  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2914d36a-6bbe-45a6-9cd2-8e077dc7686e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2609262138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15948049096373092688"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567375123i/28085596._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>You can keep the glory. I'm just here for the blood.</i>
</blockquote><b>I'm so <i>motherf*cking</i> dead right now.</b><br/><br/>Mia Corvere, once a wealthy heiress, <b>now a ruthless assassin,</b> has received her first assignment.<br/><br/> But her heart is not in her work - she only wishes to extract revenge on those who killed her family. <blockquote>
  <i>Thus, the greatest monsters get their way, she realized. By looking just like the rest of us.</i>
</blockquote> Consul Scaeva and Cardinal Duomo are responsible for her family's ruin and she will do whatever's nece</span>
  <span id="freeText15948049096373092688" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567375123i/28085596._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>You can keep the glory. I'm just here for the blood.</i>
</blockquote><b>I'm so <i>motherf*cking</i> dead right now.</b><br><br>Mia Corvere, once a wealthy heiress, <b>now a ruthless assassin,</b> has received her first assignment.<br><br> But her heart is not in her work - she only wishes to extract revenge on those who killed her family. <blockquote>
  <i>Thus, the greatest monsters get their way, she realized. By looking just like the rest of us.</i>
</blockquote> Consul Scaeva and Cardinal Duomo are responsible for her family's ruin and she will do whatever's necessary to murder them.<br><br> The Grand Games, a result of <b>the gladiatorial collegium,</b> are set to happen in Godsgrave this year and both Scaeva and Duomo are to make an appearance in person.<br><br>And so, after making excuses to the Red Church (the guild of assassins), Mia does the only logical action,<b> she sells herself into slavery</b> and takes over a collegium.<br><br> If she becomes the head gladiator of a collegium then she will be in the same arena, on the same sands, as both her targets. <blockquote>
  <i>Silver at her throat. Stone at her feet. Iron in her heart.</i>
</blockquote>But anyone can betray her, the rivals are fierce and if she is exposed, <b>everyone she knows will die. </b><br><br>But, that is a risk she is willing to take.<blockquote>
  <i>Patience, she’d tell herself, whispering the word like a prayer. If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience.</i>
</blockquote>Ohhh my gosh. I just can't, the stress! Oh the stress! *<i>breath, just breath</i>.*<br><br> In short - my heart can't take this and my head is overwhelmed.<br><br>I am <b>absolutely in love</b> with how fully fleshed out this world is - all of the little tidbits and notes about their ceremonies or other aspects of their country really brings it to life.<br><br>The plot this time around (the gladiators) was really well done, though (and this could just be me) but <b>the ending did feel a tad bit predictable</b>...but I was having SO much fun getting there that I hardly minded.<br><br>Mia is such a crazy bada** that I am seriously just blown away by her. The lengths she is willing to go - <b>nothing short of truly stunning.</b><br><br>Also, after going through so many YA novels over the years, can I mention HOW much of a RELIEF it is when you hear the characters swear.<b> It's refreshing. Motherf*cker.</b><br><br>One more thing, I love Kristoff's <b>take on books -</b> there's this: <blockquote>
  <i>The heavens grant us only one life, but through books, we live a thousand.</i>
</blockquote> and this: <blockquote>
  <i>That's the power of words; twenty six little letter can paint a whole universe.</i>
</blockquote> I just love characters that love books!<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Simply stunning - the narration was absolutely engaging and the tone was perfect. Highly recommended.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008180034" href="/book/show/32055872-godsgrave">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874032294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12611676447504820912">I’m going to go out on a limb here and say that a disappointing book is as bad as heartbreak. <br/><br/>I haven’t fully comprehended nor accepted my heartbreak yet. I think. I feel like I’ve gone through all the <b>stages of grief</b> here. <br/><br/>As I was reading this book, I was in <b>denial</b> that this book was actually boring me. I was hopeful that it would get better. That everything I loved about Nevernight would appear. That my reluctance to pick up this book would dissipate. I kept on <b>bargaining</b> with myself about it</span>
  <span id="freeText12611676447504820912" style="display:none">I’m going to go out on a limb here and say that a disappointing book is as bad as heartbreak. <br><br>I haven’t fully comprehended nor accepted my heartbreak yet. I think. I feel like I’ve gone through all the <b>stages of grief</b> here. <br><br>As I was reading this book, I was in <b>denial</b> that this book was actually boring me. I was hopeful that it would get better. That everything I loved about Nevernight would appear. That my reluctance to pick up this book would dissipate. I kept on <b>bargaining</b> with myself about it. <br>But my gut-fucking-instinct knew that this story wasn’t improving. The new relationship that flourished between Mia and that thing irritated me beyond belief. The hypocrisy of Mia when it came to not holding that thing accountable was aggravating. And then they fell in love? Based on what exactly? <br><br>Then came the stages of <b>anger</b> and <b>depression</b> and <b>bargaining</b>. My heartbreak was clouding my judgement. I wanted to blame myself that I wasn’t liking this book. I wanted to say that it was my fault that I waited this long to read this book. Would this have been different had I read this when it came out? On and on came the questions and self-doubt. <br><br>But then the anger took over again and I know this heartbreak wasn’t my fault. It’s the book. The story and I didn’t click. Mainly due to the fact that the story wasn’t right. I might have been partially to blame for some things, but most of the blame lies with the story. <br><br>And we now come to the final stage of grief, as they say. <b>Acceptance.</b> <br>Acceptance and acknowledgment that this story was a flop. And acceptance that I’m not bothering to read Darkdawn. <br><br>And now my heart is being flooded with relief. <br>——————————<br><br>So like I accidentally read the last WORD of GODSGRAVE as I was checking the page count AND I AM FREAKING THE FUCK OUT RIGHT NOW!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/623300.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159863289?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159863289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6083284227934338731"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508611036i/24235178._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevernight</a> ★★★★★<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The heavens grant us only one life, but through books, we live a thousand.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Well, I’m not entirely sure how I’m supposed to function while lying in wait for the third and final book in this series. That last chapter made me feel things that very few books are able to evoke from me. I honestly am not sure how I could possibly string together words to let you guys know how much I loved this book, but I do suppose I should at least try. <br/><br/><i>Godsgrave</i> picks up right after</span>
  <span id="freeText6083284227934338731" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508611036i/24235178._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> ★★★★★<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The heavens grant us only one life, but through books, we live a thousand.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Well, I’m not entirely sure how I’m supposed to function while lying in wait for the third and final book in this series. That last chapter made me feel things that very few books are able to evoke from me. I honestly am not sure how I could possibly string together words to let you guys know how much I loved this book, but I do suppose I should at least try. <br><br><i>Godsgrave</i> picks up right after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a>. But where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> felt like an adult <i>Harry Potter</i> (with an amazingly gothic floo powder network) where our main protagonist, Mia, is learning to become an assassin for the Red Church and the Lady of Blessed Murder, <i>Godsgrave</i> is an all-out gladiator gauntlet, where our characters are fighting to the death and only the very best may rise in rank. <br><br>Mia also has grown a lot since the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a>, and she is figuring out rather quickly that she is truly unable to trust anyone. <i>Godsgrave</i> is way more brutal and gory, but it’s also much more raw and emotional. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The choice between looking plain and pretty isn’t really a choice at all. But any fool knows looking dangerous is preferable to both.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>One of my favorite parts of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> is how Mia never explains that she is bisexual, but her actions just show it. There isn’t a big coming out story, or any explanation on why she feels the things she does for men and woman, Mia is just herself and I loved it more than words. Well, <i>Godsgrave</i> really delves into Mia’s sexuality, and it’s honestly a thing of beauty. Honestly, all I want in my adult fantasy is to read about queer girls saving their worlds, and Jay Kristoff delivered that to me better than maybe anyone else has. I will forever cherish this series for that alone. Also, I will go down with that fucking ship. OTP is an understatement. This is honestly the queer, f/f, assassins taking over the world, high fantasy, love story, I’ve been searching for my entire life. <br><br>Mia Corvere is one of my favorite characters of all time. She tries so hard to be morally grey, and I guess she truly is to most extents, but seeing her able to be soft and capable of unconditional love is something I don’t even have words for. Mia is strong, and brilliant, and clever, and brave, and everything I love in a main protagonist. And she always acknowledges how beauty, too, can be a weapon, but how important it is to never have it be your only weapon. And Mia has had so many shitty hands dealt to her, but she is able to overcome it all realistically and inspirationally. I honestly love Mia, and Mister Kindly and Eclipse also bring me more joy that I should probably admit. <br><br>Also, let me state that this book is definitely not Young Adult. Not only do I believe this is Adult Fantasy, I think it holds up to all the beloved and highly praised High Fantasy out there. This book/series can get rather dark at times, so know that going in. Also, there is a decent amount of sexual content in this book, so use caution if that makes you uncomfortable. And <b>trigger warnings</b> for violence, murder, gore, slavery, child abuse, and things along those lines. But I hope that doesn’t discourage you, because this world is amazing, these characters are perfection, the messages are beautiful, and the discourse is so damn important.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So much wealth held in so few palms. A kingdom of the blind, built on the backs of the bruised and the broken.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>From the first page to the last page, this book had me so enthralled. I loved this more than words. <i>Godsgrave</i> will easily be one of my top ten favorite books of 2017, and the third book will be all I look forward to in (hopefully) the coming year. Jay Kristoff has perfected his craft at writing, and I’d honestly do just about anything to get my hands on anything new from this world. Even though I shouldn’t give him anything, because he is now the proud owner of the heart he ripped out from me reading the ending of this book. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That's the power of words; twenty six little letters can paint a whole universe”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="6083284227934338731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer454316079828392205">I am..................................... how do you say............................. Shook<br/>With so many insane plot reveals I had trouble keeping track, a really great slow burn romance, and the most excellent lead character, this book kind of killed my soul. It’s a sequel, so we’ll split this up into sections. Let’s talk!<br/><br/><i>
  <b>→ theme work ←</b>
</i><br/>Aaaaaah, this was so great. I think this book was more focused on the fact that every single person is the hero of their own story. In the first half, I was t</span>
  <span id="freeText454316079828392205" style="display:none">I am..................................... how do you say............................. Shook<br>With so many insane plot reveals I had trouble keeping track, a really great slow burn romance, and the most excellent lead character, this book kind of killed my soul. It’s a sequel, so we’ll split this up into sections. Let’s talk!<br><br><i>
  <b>→ theme work ←</b>
</i><br>Aaaaaah, this was so great. I think this book was more focused on the fact that every single person is the hero of their own story. In the first half, I was thinking this book <i>really</i> could have done more with the discussion of slavery - like, come on - but the second half DOES that shit far better than I was expecting. <br><br><i>
  <b>→ writing ←</b>
</i><br>I think the thing that saves the writing of this book for me is that it feels like it’s laughing at itself. <b>I can feel the dilapidated, possibly soulless ghost of Jay Kristoff laughing at himself as he types these ridiculous words, and I sort of love it.</b> Every weird sentence is a reminder that this story has a narrator, a sarcastic and slightly pretentious narrator whose identity we still do not know. <br><br><i>
  <b>→ plot and twists ←</b>
</i><br>This one started sort of slow but it ended <i>brilliantly</i>. This series has a lot of battle scenes - trust me, I get it if you need to skip sections due to gore etc, I get it. The plot reveals are the best - um, my favorite was the backstory reveal and the way that worked thematically. I am so fucking sorry that I cannot say anything more than that.<br><br>also, me an uncomfortable amount of times during this book:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522308422ra/25289266.gif" width="300" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <b>→ characters ←</b>
</i><br>Miaaaaaa. I adore Mia as a character so much and I would read the series for her alone. She is such a complex and compelling antihero with such a complex and nuanced arc. I never know if she’s going to swerve evil or good, but I know I’m desperately invested in who she becomes. <b>
  <u>I love that she does evil things with good intentions and toes that line.</u>
</b><br><br><i>
  <b>→ romance ←</b>
</i><br>Ash and Mia are the GREATEST. They have this friends-to-enemies-to-lovers slow-burn dynamic I basically adore. Uh… yeah. I really love the juxtaposition of them to other romantic relationships as being far healthier, even though they’re both literal assassins?<br><br><i>
  <b>→ more thoughts ←</b>
</i><br>The cissexism is really bothersome? I mean, it feels like every two chapters there’s some mention of vaginas vs. dicks and like… I get that you like being Gritty and Dark, but what am I reading. I also think occasionally the Grittiness overpowers the plot. Which I dislike. That part is bad and I dislike it. <br><br><i>
  <b>→ enjoyment factor ←</b>
</i><br>I don't even know, guys, these are just so addicting. I always have trouble getting into the beginning but from there, <b>I just enjoy every second I spend reading these</b>. This book took a while to get started, but once it got going, it became a straight-up [gay-up] masterpiece of plot twists and of character development. And I adore it. <br><br>and, to end this all off:<br><b>
  <i>→ spoilery theories, look away now ←</i>
</b><br>there’s some narrative of the fall of Ashkahi Empire, the crown of the moon, and the monstrosities left behind being connected<br>Mia being able to summon Sand Krackens is going to be super relevant. <span id="freeTextContainer4678226476392746506"><b>5 Stars</b> <br/>(And I'm being stingy with these this year, so this is a big deal, gentle friends.)<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532036705ra/25999258.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I originally marked this as 4+ stars.<br/>But after further consideration of the following:<br/><br/>1) I read this book in ONE sitting because I was so spellbound. <br/>And, 2) I re-read my review for book one and realized that ALL the things I said I couldn't stand about book one, I adored about book two...<br/><br/>I decided to say, fuck it, 5 stars for everyone, folks. And because good on you, Sir Kristoff. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532036705ra/25999259.gif' width='500' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>He really is a creative </span>
  <span id="freeText4678226476392746506" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b> <br>(And I'm being stingy with these this year, so this is a big deal, gentle friends.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532036705ra/25999258.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I originally marked this as 4+ stars.<br>But after further consideration of the following:<br><br>1) I read this book in ONE sitting because I was so spellbound. <br>And, 2) I re-read my review for book one and realized that ALL the things I said I couldn't stand about book one, I adored about book two...<br><br>I decided to say, fuck it, 5 stars for everyone, folks. And because good on you, Sir Kristoff. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532036705ra/25999259.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He really is a creative talent. <br><br>Now, if you read my review for book one (which you can find <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097135993" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>), you will see that - while I enjoyed the overall story itself - I had problems with Kristoff's almost satirical, dark humor style and his employment of footnotes as a narration tool. <br><br>For those who don't feel like checking out that review (and who could blame you) or haven't read the books, here's a picture I jacked from it for reference of said footnotes:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515361550i/24855204._SY540_.jpg" width="282" height="376" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, perhaps it was the fact that I went into this book <i>prepared</i> for those things...or perhaps more aptly, I just went in to this one <i>understanding</i> Kristoff's style and thus - now unclouded by confusion and its subsequent resistance - I was able to just absorb the story and its characters. <br><br>Either way, I just enjoyed the shit out of this book.<br><br>It's original and edgy and weird and bloody and violent and I loved it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532036705ra/25999260.gif" width="344" height="378" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And - after that ending - I can't fucking WAIT for book three. <br><br>And now - after once considering tossing both books without even cracking book two open - I find myself fighting not to re-purchase book one in hardcover. I have it in paperback and it doesn't match my book two hardcover (and future book three hardcover). <br><br>Because, well...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532036705ra/25999261.gif" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes, yes, I know. <br>#ShamelessBookHoarderIssues<br><br>We can't all be perfect. <br>And thank fuck.</span>

    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2783597276?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008180034" href="/book/show/32055872-godsgrave">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review">reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2783597276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16935422537774078619">Jay Kristoff is an absolute master storyteller. This is such an exceedingly well-balanced novel in all its grandness. I expected some of the momentum to dwindle, as often is the case with the second book in a series, though this retained its sharp edge. And boy does it sting! <br/><br/>He is not afraid to kill off characters. He is not afraid to destroy friendships and watch his heroes crumble into the dust. And he certainly isn’t afraid to take his book in new and exciting directions. Mia spent most of t</span>
  <span id="freeText16935422537774078619" style="display:none">Jay Kristoff is an absolute master storyteller. This is such an exceedingly well-balanced novel in all its grandness. I expected some of the momentum to dwindle, as often is the case with the second book in a series, though this retained its sharp edge. And boy does it sting! <br /><br />He is not afraid to kill off characters. He is not afraid to destroy friendships and watch his heroes crumble into the dust. And he certainly isn’t afraid to take his book in new and exciting directions. Mia spent most of the novel training to be a gladiator, an ingenious ruse in order to get close to her intended target. It a long-drawn-out game, one that completely changed her perspective on exactly who she is and what she wants from the world. There’s more to this assassin than murder, much more. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But those who stand for nothing die for the same. And if you stand only for yourself, you fall alone.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Some parts of this had an almost cinematic quality to them. The arena fights were so massive and well-orchestrated that I couldn’t help but imagine them on the screen (or as part of the actual audience in the stadium.) And that says a lot to me because the way he writes is just so damn exquisite. The prose flows beautifully from word to word, from sentence to sentence. The fight scenes are spectacular. And the sex, well, that’s on an entirely different level. Some authors avoid writing about it, closing the scene as the action is about to ensue. Some authors do terribly clumsy jobs attempting to describe it, and some make it seem quite real on the page. Jay Kristoff, on the other hand, writes the best sex scenes in fantasy. (It has to be said.) It was done so well, so organically, and that’s all I’m going to say about that. I’m impressed with the level of emotion he managed to get on the page here in both forms of action, so to speak. <br /><br />This series has everything I could ever want in fantasy: a rich world, conflicted characters, assassins, dark magic and a protagonist that is strong, clever and necessarily brutal. It’s the dark magic haunting her steps that is slowly pushing the series forward. As Mia is trying to plan the downfall of the two most powerful men in the world, and as the Ministry of the Red Church are trying to guide her blades for their own ends, her magic is becoming stronger and more complete. Her shadows are becoming darker as she absorbs more power from slain Darkin. By series end she will have everything her mysterious destiny demands and where this all takes her will be quite the shocker, I have no doubt. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Patience, she’d tell herself, whispering the word like a prayer. If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Godsgrave completely exceeded my expectations. I thought I knew where this was all going but I really didn’t have a clue. Darkdawn, the final book in the trilogy, is out later this year and I can’t wait to read it. This ended on such a monumental cliff-hanger. If Jay Kristoff writes with the same level of imagination and originality as he has here, this could be one of the best trilogies fantasy has ever seen. <br /><br />_________________________________<br /><br />You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br />__________________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="16935422537774078619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2696621023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696621023" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2696621023?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34326424-godsgrave">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696621023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2957769240494473796"><b>I applaud The Droogs who finished <i>Godsgrave</i> before or around its publication date, thank you for your sacrifice; may the Lady of Blessed Murder bless your patience.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“That's the power of words; twenty six little letter can paint a whole universe” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/><i>Godsgrave</i> is the sequel to <i>Nevernight</i>. The story still follows our beloved ruthless assassin, Mia Corvere, as she continues her journey for vengeance. <i>Godsgrave</i> didn’t start off easy for me to get into. <i>Nevernight</i> was a revenge story with a ba</span>
  <span id="freeText2957769240494473796" style="display:none"><b>I applaud The Droogs who finished <i>Godsgrave</i> before or around its publication date, thank you for your sacrifice; may the Lady of Blessed Murder bless your patience.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“That's the power of words; twenty six little letter can paint a whole universe” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>Godsgrave</i> is the sequel to <i>Nevernight</i>. The story still follows our beloved ruthless assassin, Mia Corvere, as she continues her journey for vengeance. <i>Godsgrave</i> didn’t start off easy for me to get into. <i>Nevernight</i> was a revenge story with a battle-school setting; <i>Godsgrave</i> is the continuation to that revenge story without any of the battle-school trope. Almost the entirety of the book revolved around a new mission: Mia’s struggle to win the gladiatorial collegium for a chance to complete her unfinished revenge. Although familiar faces and characters—such as Mister Kindly and Eclipse—still played a huge role, many previous characters only appeared briefly; there were a lot of new characters introduced in this installment and for the majority of the time, Mia spent her time with them rather than the characters from the first book. Also, I’ve mentioned in my <i>Nevernight</i> review that the footnotes didn’t bother me; they were entertaining and they provided insights into the world-building of Itreya. This is still true in <i>Godsgrave</i>, but admittedly, the footnotes in this installment were often too long to my liking. I’m talking about one or two pages long footnotes. The longevity of the footnotes ended up being distracting to my reading immersion, and this was especially true in the first half of the book. Because of all these, <i>Godsgrave</i> ended up taking me longer—around 40% of the book—to fully engross myself into. Were all this necessary though? Yes. Rest assured that the build-up and groundwork were put to good use; resulting in an incredibly engaging second half of the book.<br><br><b>Picture: <i>Pale Daughter</i> by Nan Fe</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567245126i/28078801._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s true that it took me a while to warm up to the characters introduced in this installment, but in the second half of the book, I ended up caring about their fates and lives more than I expected due to the interactions that Mia had with them in the first half. In my opinion, the characters’ banter in <i>Godsgrave</i> were better than <i>Nevernight</i>; Mister Kindly and Eclipse non-stop bickering was simply so damn fun. I’ve said this before, but Mia Corvere is a great heroine to read; this middle book of a trilogy develop her character even more. Kristoff never stops putting Mia in a difficult situation where she had to choose between saving her friends or putting her revenge as the single main priority. Genuine feelings were displayed as she tries her best to conquer the internal conflicts warring with her. By this point, it’s safe to say that she’s a very well-realized character; I may not agree with some of her decisions—I personally think Mia’s choice of romance doesn’t deserve her love after the events that occurred in the first book—but it felt believable and true to her personality, that’s what matters most.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Problem with being a librarian is there's some lessons you just can't learn from books.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>On Twitter and Instagram, I’ve seen videos of people throwing their copies of <i>Godsgrave</i> across the room or outside their window after they finished the book; this is a truly understandable response. <i>Godsgrave</i> concluded in a fashion that demands readers to have the next installment ready because it ended on a massive cliffhanger; those who waited two years of waiting for <i>Darkdawn</i> to be released after such a brutal cliffhanger of intensity must’ve experienced a torturous period of time. The final pages in <i>Godsgrave</i> were simply remarkable. Seriously, every chapter in the last quarter seems to escalate the problems and stakes for Mia and her friends further and further. The drama and the cinematic set pieces within the salvos of revelations and bloodbath were constantly gripping and thrilling; showing Kristoff’s skill as a storyteller magnificently.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“She'd grown up inside books. No matter how dark life became, shutting out the hurt was as easy as opening a cover. A child of murdered parents and a failed rebellion, she'd still walked in the boots of scholars and warriors, queens and conquerors.<br><br>The heavens grant us only one life, but through books, we live a thousand.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The insanely high average ratings on Goodreads speaks for the quality of the book. <i>Godsgrave</i> takes its time for the plot to get going in order to make sure that the second-half gives an exhilarating reading experience. There weren’t many revelations regarding Darkin and Mia’s ability; the unnamed narrator has mentioned that the final pieces of the puzzle will be revealed in <i>Darkdawn</i>, and I consider myself fortunate that I only have to wait for a few days before I can read it. <br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9781250073037/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/08/31/book-review-godsgrave-the-nevernight-chronicle-2-by-jay-kristoff/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2957769240494473796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Friends, Romans, and Countrymen</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2425712563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6832449387546108802"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533824847ra/26101876.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>That's right, folks. We've transitioned from assassins to gladiators!</b><br/>Now, some of you will (like me) love this, but some of you? <br/><i>Ehhhhh.</i> Maybe not so much...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507888565ra/24159503.gif' width='400' height='170' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Personally, I loved the way Kristoff mixed it up this time around. There was <i>pseudo</i>-Roman empire feel to the setting of the story in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1817949745' rel='nofollow noopener'>first book</a>, so (to me) this was a natural progression of that same story. But I can see how some might find the transition jarring<br/>because my mind doesn't <b>
  <i>automatically</i>
</b> translate ninja assassins</span>
  <span id="freeText6832449387546108802" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533824847ra/26101876.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>That's right, folks. We've transitioned from assassins to gladiators!</b><br>Now, some of you will (like me) love this, but some of you? <br><i>Ehhhhh.</i> Maybe not so much...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507888565ra/24159503.gif" width="400" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Personally, I loved the way Kristoff mixed it up this time around. There was <i>pseudo</i>-Roman empire feel to the setting of the story in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1817949745" rel="nofollow noopener">first book</a>, so (to me) this was a natural progression of that same story. But I can see how some might find the transition jarring<br>because my mind doesn't <b>
  <i>automatically</i>
</b> translate ninja assassins into gladiators, either.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530966393ra/25937427.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Regardless of the setting, I felt like Mia's character remained consistent, and that was really the most important thing for me. I thought the change in scenery was an extremely interesting pivot for a second book to take and, to me, the story benefitted from it quite a bit.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533828667ra/26102221.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Again, that's just my personal take on it. <br>Speaking of personal preferences, for those who found the silly<i>ish</i> footnotes annoying and/or weird? If you didn't like them before, you probably still won't like them. <br><b>BUT.</b> &lt;--and I have no data to back this up<br>It seemed like there were <i>less</i> of them this time around. Now, considering the fact that I <i>did</i> like them and thought they were a funny way to break up any monotony, you may want to take that with a grain of salt. I wasn't exactly taking notes for my extensive data collection about the footnotes.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533913539ra/26106223.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So how <i>does</i> Mia end up fighting in an arena?<br>Well, she sells herself into slavery, of course!<br>And <i>why the fuck</i> would she ever do something like that?<br>Well, <i>I'm</i> sure as hell not going to tell you. I mean, that would ruin the story, don't you think?<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533830656ra/26102343.gif" width="400" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I can tell you is that Mia continues to be a badass, the old <i>and</i> new characters continue to be amazingly 3 dimensional, and the plot continues to thicken.<br><b>Highly recommended.</b></span>

<div id="review_2383612343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2383612343" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2383612343?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2383612343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5889332209097775690"><i> “When you take a person out of the world, you don't just take them, do you? <br/>You take everything they were, too.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>A short summary of what happens in the book: <br/>Sex and murder (yes, at the same time), fight, train, Gladiatii, kill, fight, train, murder, sex, intrigues, fight, murder, surprise, kill, fight and brutal plot twists.<br/>That left me like this:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443042991ra/16309709.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Whereas the first book was concentrated in the school for killing (that’s my personal name for it...) this book played in the arenas</span>
  <span id="freeText5889332209097775690" style="display:none"><i> “When you take a person out of the world, you don't just take them, do you? <br>You take everything they were, too.” </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>A short summary of what happens in the book: <br>Sex and murder (yes, at the same time), fight, train, Gladiatii, kill, fight, train, murder, sex, intrigues, fight, murder, surprise, kill, fight and brutal plot twists.<br>That left me like this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443042991ra/16309709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Whereas the first book was concentrated in the school for killing (that’s my personal name for it...) this book played in the arenas of the gladiatii. <br>All in all this is a masterpiece! <br>Brilliant. Jay Kristoff is a genius for writing and creating this story! <br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>So much lovable characters in this one! <br>I mean... they’re all killers but kind of lovable? <br>Do I sound crazy? Probably. <br>Is it still true? Yes. <br>Starting with my favorite killer in the world: talented blade, bisexual bomb and super badass Mia. <br>She’s so skilled and intelligent. <br>All the thoughts and emotions she felt made her so real and human. <br>Next are her awesome partners in crime lurking in the shadows. <br>Mr. Kindly and Eclipse. <br>I said it once, I say it again: can I have darklin powers and followers aka friends like those two? <br>I mean, yes, they don’t get along well, but the “fights” they have are absolutely hilarious and I loved them for it.<br>But if anyone ever asked me which one is my favorite, it’ll always be Mr. Kindly. <br>Because, duh, a cat. <br>A shadow cat. <br>Absolutely-freakin-awesome. <br>Next is Furian: I wasn’t sure about him if I’m truly honest. He was a little bit interesting but the major part of it I felt like he was just a part of the book the author needed to put in there. Buuuuut... That’s just my opinion. <br>Sid: This fluffy big mouth guy was one of my favorites. As soon as he showed his real face he was the absolute best with his humor, his stupid words and kind heart. <br>All the other characters were created in a really brilliant way, because it didn’t matter how small their role was: if they died or were killed I was really sad about it... <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>When I first met Mia in Nevernight I was really intrigued by the talent or power that made Mia a darklin. <br>I was always fascinated by shadows, darkness. They do have a huge power in the world. Just look at the Darkling in the shadow and bone series. He was pretty powerful. <br>But this Darklin-power is different. It has some positive sides but also negative sides. <br>In the end the universe is in balance, right? <br>Next to these awesome powers there are beasts that sound like the worst nightmare ever and people that make you really uncomfortable.<br>In the world of the gladiatii There is only one way to earn your freedom. Kill everyone in the magni and survive as the last one standing. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Oh well. This was one hot thing. All the tension, all the heat, all the passion, (all the hatred). <br>I knew it would end in some way. I hoped it would be a good way. <br>And oh my good, guys, smut scenes. <br>Puh-huh. Get some ice cream because the scenes in this book are smoking hot! <br>Also... the friendships made my heart feel some things and my face smile. <br>Even if you need to kill for a living, when you’re surrounded by the same people for months, in some way they start to be your family. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>The most important thing first: People who hate curse-filled-books should probably leave this book in the bookstore shelf and never touch it. <br>Because this one is filled with heavy language. <br>And you know what? <br>I loved it. <br>It’s some fresh air in a normally really organized and strict book writing factory. <br>Also: Jay Kristoff writes really good fighting-/killing-/love making-scenes. <br>And he’s definitely a master in plot twists! <br>So. Definitely one of my favorite series of all time! So addictive and different. Read it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5889332209097775690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095672243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12831120494880250813">I don’t know where to begin with this review???<br/>I mean I think i’ve already mentioned everything I needed to say in my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_' title='Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevernight</a>…<br/><br/><b>Either way, to recap and reciprocate the points I mentioned in <i>Nevernight’s</i> review, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23264671.Godsgrave__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___2_' title='Godsgrave (The Nevernight Chronicle, #2) by Jay Kristoff' rel='nofollow noopener'>Godsgrave</a> had even more witty banters. more blood. more pain. lots of angst. plentiful twists. the suspense could give you a clean kill, and even more traumatic than its prequel.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504624563i/23793848.jpg' width='“400”' height='“225”' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Tbh the moment I was done with this book, I almost gave into my weak mind telling me I was wrong to</span>
  <span id="freeText12831120494880250813" style="display:none">I don’t know where to begin with this review???<br>I mean I think i’ve already mentioned everything I needed to say in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a>…<br><br><b>Either way, to recap and reciprocate the points I mentioned in <i>Nevernight’s</i> review, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23264671.Godsgrave__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___2_" title="Godsgrave (The Nevernight Chronicle, #2) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a> had even more witty banters. more blood. more pain. lots of angst. plentiful twists. the suspense could give you a clean kill, and even more traumatic than its prequel.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504624563i/23793848.jpg" width="“400”" height="“225”" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tbh the moment I was done with this book, I almost gave into my weak mind telling me I was wrong to read this so early on especially because book 3 doesn’t have a publication date yet, let alone a freakin title. If you think for one second to dive into this book without being aware that there is a major cliffhanger in the end, I wish you the best of luck! So please take your poor heart into consideration before jumping in, okay? 🙂<br><br>Remember how I previously mentioned that this book is even more gruesome than it's predecessor? Well, we’re introduced to new characters in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23264671.Godsgrave__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___2_" title="Godsgrave (The Nevernight Chronicle, #2) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a> as this book continues where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> left us off with. <b>New characters aka more deaths, you get it 🙂</b> There’s nothing different about the format used, we have the story told to us in past and present tense but this time it’s spiced up a bit with the past tense being Mia post-Red Church and the present: 3 months post-Red Church. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mia is assigned to a new task as an official Blade of Lady of the Blessed Mother <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Mia takes up a new task assigned by the Red Church and travels to Godsgrave to bid herself to become a slave of Leona (daughter of a shitty dude in the Senate, his name is irrelevant). There she meets other slaves and all of them have to fight with each other in a bunch of bloody contests (in public because hello, it’s <i>fun</i>) set out by the Senate (<i>she tried not to care about them but hahahah</i>). <b>The last one standing will be free from slavery foreveerrrrrrr</b>. That said, her mind didn’t drift from wanting to avenge her father’s death so the closer she is to where she once belonged, the better she can get both jobs done. However, there’s a plot twist here and a plot twist there and a plot twist everywhere and as a requirement by sir Jay Kristoff, things just don’t go as planned 🙂 <br><br>I don’t want to dive in to the characters as I feel it’s best to go in blind but note that you’re going to love them all, even if they suck. To conclude, this book is um great. it’s um the best and um brace yourselves in the last 10% of the book because it could damage chunks of your brain cells in one go. I’m out 👋<br><br><i>special shoutout to cuteamy who was buddy reading this with me. thank you for pushing me to read while i was in a weird slump, it was so worth it and one of the best br experiences i’ve had in forever. and most of all, thank you for holding your screams in so that i could catch up to you, it must have been really painful lol</i><br><br><br> **********<br><br><i>imshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshakingimshaking</i><br><br><b>BUDDY READ</b> with my bodyguard, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61624004-amy" rel="nofollow noopener">cuteamy</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1582228343" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1582228343" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582228343?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34326424-godsgrave">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=not-your-ordinary-creatures">not-your-ordinary-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=that-bastard">that-bastard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=riddikulus">riddikulus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=revolting">revolting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=that-bitch-is-cray">that-bitch-is-cray</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=assassins">assassins</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582228343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8535032879147125760"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Last year, NEVERNIGHT, the first book in Jay Kristoff's NEVERNIGHT CHRONICLE, was at the top of my Best Books of 2016 list. The writing was brilliant, the story and characters compelling, the world-building was fantastic . . . I was smitten. <br/><br/>So I was understandably excited about its sequel GODSGRAVE. *sighs*<br/><br/>BUT.<br/><br/>The story was still compelling, just <i>not as</i> compelling, the writing was likewise <i>not as </i>brilliant, and the old characters manifested new flaws while several of the new characters</span>
  <span id="freeText8535032879147125760" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Last year, NEVERNIGHT, the first book in Jay Kristoff's NEVERNIGHT CHRONICLE, was at the top of my Best Books of 2016 list. The writing was brilliant, the story and characters compelling, the world-building was fantastic . . . I was smitten. <br><br>So I was understandably excited about its sequel GODSGRAVE. *sighs*<br><br>BUT.<br><br>The story was still compelling, just <i>not as</i> compelling, the writing was likewise <i>not as </i>brilliant, and the old characters manifested new flaws while several of the new characters were downright contemptible.<br><br>It took awhile for all of these slightly lesser versions to fully establish themselves, so initially I was more hopeful . . . Which only served to make the eventual disappointment that much worse.<br><br>For example, I love all things gladiatorial (b/c bloodthirsty). The obstacles, the arena atmosphere, the fighting to the death, be it man vs. man or man vs. beast, I don't care, I LOVE ALL OF IT. *laughs maniacally*<br><br>So when it became clear that Mia's endgame was dependent on her becoming enslaved and entering the arena, I did a happy dance in celebration . . . A celebration that turned out to be premature . . . B/c boring.<br><br><b>You:</b> Shut up, nothing about arena fights-to-the-death is boring.<br><br><b>Me:</b> One would think . . . And one would be mistaken.<br><br><b>You:</b> *taps foot impatiently* Explain.<br><br><b>Me:</b> Only one of the four fights resembled anything like traditional gladiator fighting <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and it was a 3:1 fight against a seven foot tall humanoid arachnid, and I don't like things with more than four legs (even when they're normal sized). It's a rule. <br><br>SPEAKING OF RULES, I have a new one: NO KILLING ONE HALF OF A PAIR OF TWINS (which should've been made a rule when I read HARRY POTTER, but I didn't have rules back then, and this is the first time it's happened since). *wails*  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Okay, <i>two</i> of them, but chariot races are the least fun part of arena fights. <br><br>I've never been much for going in circles--I don't like NASCAR either--and shooting arrows at targets and people while you do it doesn't make it any more entertaining. As for the other fights, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[one of them was a battle reenactment complete with siege engines and catapults, and the other was a full-out NAVAL BATTLE. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>It was more spectacle than fight, and yes, arena fights are spectacles, but that's not <em>all</em> they are. At least, that's not all they're supposed to be. <br><br>Kristoff didn't get that memo.<br><br>The lackluster arena action was made worse by one of the aforementioned newly developed character flaws: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[CHEATING.<br><br>I'm not talking about Mia using her darkinness. I don't consider using a natural ability to be cheating. But dosing the water supply with narcotics and using some kind of science voodoo to make your opponent's obsidian swords even more breakable? <br><br>That's the kind of cheap shit that's supposed to separate the Good Guys from the Bad Guys. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Another issue I had with Mia was that she seemed to have regressed into a hormone-addled adolescent:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Peering in through the door, she saw Dona Leona emerging from a deep, steaming pool, water running in rivulets down her bare body. Her hair was damp, her face bereft of paint. It occurred to Mia that she was a beauty; full hips and fuller lips. <b>Her eyes roamed Leona’s curves</b>, wreathed in steam, and she wondered at the thrill of it. Why, downstairs in the barracks, seeing naked bodies meant nothing, but here, her skin was prickling. Heart beating faster. <b>Thinking, perhaps, of another beauty on Aurelius’s bed</b>, her taste on the young don’s mouth, her golden kisses sinking ever lower. <br><b>She thought of Ashlinn</b>, then. The kiss they’d shared when Mia left the Church. That kiss that lasted a moment too long. Maybe not long enough?</i>
</blockquote><br>And this was not a one or even a threetime thing. It was an over-and-over-again thing. <br><br>BUT. <br><br>GODSGRAVE wasn't terrible. There were lots of new clues about darkins and gods and prophecies, and something we were all hoping for did indeed come to pass, but in a completely unexpected way. And Kristoff excels at giving you information without revealing an iota more than necessary, effectively keeping you on his hook. So not an even remotely bad read . . . Just not on the same level as the experience that was NEVERNIGHT, comparatively speaking. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>1/10/17:</b><br><br>We have a title, cha-cha-cha! We have a title, cha-cha-cha! *is lonely in conga line of one* But who cares? B/c GODSGRAVE. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484071886ra/21679936.gif" width="500" height="185" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8535032879147125760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2078343524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2078343524" />
    <a title="sofia (sam willows)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55057635-sofia-sam-willows"><img alt="sofia (sam willows)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579348857p2/55057635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2078343524?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sofia (sam willows)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sofia (sam willows)" href="/user/show/55057635-sofia-sam-willows">sofia (sam willows)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=couples-i-like">couples-i-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55057635-sofia-sam-willows?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2078343524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5453580153484010456">my new review after my 4th reread:<br/><br/>godsgrave starts almost a year after nevernight, with mia setting her plan to avenge her familia in motion. but there is quite a significant gap of information between the last scene in nevernight and the first scene in godsgrave, with mia in the desert. so, to bridge that gap, the first third of the story is told in alternating timelines, which adds to the main plotline in a frankly genius way. the information is revealed gradually, and kept me on the edge of m</span>
  <span id="freeText5453580153484010456" style="display:none">my new review after my 4th reread:<br /><br />godsgrave starts almost a year after nevernight, with mia setting her plan to avenge her familia in motion. but there is quite a significant gap of information between the last scene in nevernight and the first scene in godsgrave, with mia in the desert. so, to bridge that gap, the first third of the story is told in alternating timelines, which adds to the main plotline in a frankly genius way. the information is revealed gradually, and kept me on the edge of my seat trying to find out information our characters already knew. in my opinion, that did wonders for the buildup of tension in the beginning, something that was severely lacking in book 1.<br /><br />besides that, another thing that's greatly improved in godsgrave is our main character, mia. i love mia so fucking much in al her flaws and complexities, but we can all agree that my girl is kind of a hypocrite. she blames people for killing people she likes in the name of revenge while literally murdering hundreds to avenge her family. to say that her moral compass is skewed would be an understatement. but in godsgrave, instead of following her vengeance blindly, she begins to question if it's all really worth it, and if the people she kills along the way deserve it. it's honestly one of my favorite character arcs <i>ever</i>. how at first she put herself on an unreachable pedestal of superior morality with her reasoning that scaeva, remus and duomo must die, while judging everyone else who does the same, to questioning who she is what made her become like that, if her revenge and everything she's done to achieve it are really worth it, and if it's really a good excuse for her actions and cruelty. i absolutely love her journey, and darkdawn wraps it up even more beautifully.<br /><br />besides nailing the characterization of mia and the pacing, godsgrave also takes the action to a whole new level. instead of training with swords like in nevernight, now mia's swordsmanship is put to the test with actual gladiator battles. they're brutal, bloody, and beautiful. the action is not only more interesting, it's also more consistent throughout the book, having high-stakes fight scenes from the beginning to the end. there are so many battles here that are frankly <i>iconic</i>, and so fucking awesome, that i truly believe they are some of the best out there in the fantasy genre.<br /><br />there is so much more that i could say about godsgrave, but 99.99% of it would just be praise. it's no secret i love this book with all my soul, but not everybody does. in fact, the nevernight series (and especially book 1), although being very hyped, is very polarizing, and has received some very legitimate criticism. one complaint that this series frequently receives is about the writing: how it's pretentious, or too flowery, or the footnotes too distracting. and to be honest, whether that bothers you or not is purely based on personal preference. but i can say without a doubt that if you had problems with those aspects in nevernight, you'll definitely enjoy godsgrave more, as we as readers are already established in the world and familiar with the tone, and the author doesn't have to go out of their way to tell you how this book and story work, so the writing turns out not as in-your-face. <br /><br />i could honestly write a master thesis on why this book is a masterpiece, but i'm afraid i would be the only one interested. so i'll leave this review like this: <b>the nevernight chronicle has its flaws and its shortcomings, and not everybody enjoys it. but if you think there's a slight chance you might enjoy it, that you might come to love this series just a fraction of how much i do, then please, <u>read this series.</u></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5453580153484010456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5814168334516634458" style="display:none"><b>F U C K.</b> ME. <br /><br />And I <i>

  <i>screams for days</i>
</b>*<br /><br /><b>(I was going to do a review on my channel, but I'm waiting for the UK edition to arrive so I can show all of you how <i>beautiful</i> it is, so once I do, I'll leave a link to it down below.)</b><br /><br />I think this book surpassed <b>all of my expectations and brought them up to an all new high</b>. It was so, <i>so</i> good. Again, Jay's writing was excellent, full of buttery prose and lyrical pieces. This time around though, I didn't mind the footnotes. With the first book, I was mildly annoyed and somewhat irritated but then I got used to it and by the time the <i>Godsgrave</i> came around, I was so interested and more invested in the story, I flew through <i>E V E R Y T H I N G</i>. <br /><br />With <b>twice more</b> the action, blood, guts, violence, gore, and badassery, I really recommend you give this series (trilogy) a go. It's bloody fucking awesome and with the twists and unexpected surprises that this book has, your head will literally implode from all the insanity. <br /><br />But really, <b>R E A L L Y</b>, Mr. Kristoff, that cruel, <i>c r u e l</i>, ending.<br />I see you. <b>I see you.</b> And how I hate you (relatively speaking). <br /><br /><b>5 BLOODY KICKASS STARS</b><br /><br /><i>Arc provided by author/publisher in exchange for an honest review</i>.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/branbookaddict" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/brandonthebookaddict/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookstagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/brandonthebookaddict" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> |</span>
