    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1726701831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1726701831" />
    <a title="Delirious Disquisitions" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5831406-delirious-disquisitions"><img alt="Delirious Disquisitions" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600382655p2/5831406.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1726701831?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Delirious Disquisitions" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Delirious Disquisitions" href="/user/show/5831406-delirious-disquisitions">Delirious Disquisitions</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831406-delirious-disquisitions?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1726701831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14175557744236727798"><b>You should read this if you like: </b> murder, stabbings, multiple murder via stabbings, devious girls, assassins, Hogwarts School of Assassins, bisexual protagonists, sexy times, murder during sexy times, multiple plot twists, adrenaline rush that feels kind of like a heart attack, shadow cats, shadow wolves, way too much sarcasm, and more stabbings. <br/> <br/>I’m going to preface this review with a little note about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4735144.Jay_Kristoff' title='Jay Kristoff' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jay Kristoff</a>. I love him, I really do. He is one of my current favorite YA authors and on a</span>
  <span id="freeText14175557744236727798" style="display:none"><b>You should read this if you like: </b> murder, stabbings, multiple murder via stabbings, devious girls, assassins, Hogwarts School of Assassins, bisexual protagonists, sexy times, murder during sexy times, multiple plot twists, adrenaline rush that feels kind of like a heart attack, shadow cats, shadow wolves, way too much sarcasm, and more stabbings. <br /> <br />I’m going to preface this review with a little note about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4735144.Jay_Kristoff" title="Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Jay Kristoff</a>. I love him, I really do. He is one of my current favorite YA authors and on a very short list of authors I would love to meet in person someday. His books are always fantastic, with their badass heroines, impossible quests, snarky banter, and lots of action. A Kristoff book is one that’s bound to be chock full of metaphors and melodrama. And above all else, they are always, always entertaining. <br /> <br />Which is why I tend to buy and binge read them the day they are released. And you know what? Sleep deprivation riding on an adrenaline high is, ideally, the best state in which to read his books. Everything feels so much more epic and urgent; it’s all one big adrenaline rush from start to finish. Down in one shot like fine whiskey, burning all the way to the end. <br /><br />Incidentally this was the first time I read one of his books the regular way and actually took my time (a ridiculous amount of time really. It took me over two weeks) to read this book. And well, did not hold so good under scrutiny.<br /><br /><b>The plot:</b> One of the reasons I was so freaking excited about this book was because of the way things were left off in book one. It seemed to me that by murdering someone not assigned by the Red Church, Mia had summarily cut her ties to them and was now free to go off into the world and seek revenge. I was very interested to see to see where things would go from there. And boy, the first half of this book not disappoint. <br /><br />We start off with bloody murder, with our heroine smack dab in the middle of things with her revenge plot well underway. From then, we weave back and forth between the present and the past, in what is one of my favorite narrative styles, as we try to piece together the events that lead Mia to this point in the story. <br /><br />This aspect of Kristoff’s writing is something that I really love. He masterfully parallels both narratives in such a way that the stakes in one timeline is informed and then intensified by events in the other. It’s some really stuff right there! In fact, everything leading up to the first half of the book, is pretty damn epic! It’s only in the second half that the plot starts to go downhill. <br /><br />At the end of <i>Nevernight</i>, there is still so much we don’t know about Mia and where her powers originate from. I had hoped <i>Godsgrave</i> would answer some of these questions. And yet, beyond a couple mentions of Mia’s power in the beginning and some cryptic hints at the very end, the book doesn’t address any of the questions I had regarding Mia’s powers. <br /><br />The main plot of <i>Godsgrave</i> is set up for some gladiator style hunger games which gives Mia plenty of opportunities to bloody things up. This is the first time that Mia has been alone and without (many) allies and it was very entertaining to watch her plan things out as she goes. One of the best things about her character is that for all her badassery she is not infallible; something that we are constantly reminded of in this book. Despite being an assassin of the Red Church, she is not automatically proficient in all fighting techniques no is she the best at defense; which makes sense since the acolytes of the Red Church are basically thieves and murderers and only know basic fighting techniques in case they need to fight their way out when on a job. <br /><br />Therefore, Mia learning the Gladiatii style of combat and merging it with her own cunning and intellect was one of the plot highlights. The fights themselves were very creative and reminiscent of the one between The Mountain and Oberyn from Game of Thrones. However, I soon started losing interest as they started to get repetitive and seemed to drag on forever! There was so much of the fighting going on when all I could think of was that it’s a waste of time better spent learning more about her powers and how to use them. <br /><br /><b>Characters:</b> Speaking of powers, I was actually very excited to learn there was someone else who shared Mia’s powers. Furian started off as a potentially strong character. To learn that he has chosen to shun his powers thinking them abhorrent, instead of using them like Mia, was such an intriguing concept. And yet, we get nothing substantial out of his character. Furian spends the whole book alternating between a red herring love interest and a colossal pain in the ass! So much time is spent hammering on Mia and Furian’s lust/hate relationship. And yet, his only real purpose in the book is to serve as a foil for Mia. Which would have been very interesting had we gotten to explore their diverging ideologies, moralities, or motives and how that shapes their characters and relationships with the people around them. I wanted reluctant friendships! Barring that, I wanted begrudging acceptance of the other’s ways. At the very least, I wanted training montages! But instead, we get disapproving Furian who, by the way, is one half of the most annoying characters in this damn book! He spends the entire book glaring daggers at Mia and fuming in disapproval or reproaching her character. I get it. Mia’s not a good person. But damn it, if she isn’t a billion times more interesting than Furian! <br /><br />Which is not to say that I don’t want people disapproving of our protagonist. She’s an assassin! Of course someone needs to question her character. I want to see Mia being questioned and prodded and poked at. I want her to question her own intentions. Especially in light of the reveal about Mia’s family, which I thought was an excellent plot twist. I want to see that Mia be the lowest of the low and still somehow find a way to redeem herself to the readers. <br /><br />What I don’t want is to root for Mia at the cost of someone else’s character development. Make me like Mia, by making her flawed; by making her human. Not by making everyone else around her turn out to be a complete moron! <br /><br />This happens not just in Furian’s case, but also for Donna and Arkades. All three of these characters start off very strong, driven characters. All three of them are later revealed to be weak, pathetic, fools driven my childish motives and love/lust for the other. Donna is a spoiled brat seeking revenge on her father with no means of actually accomplishing them. She talks big and yet her actions make her seems very silly and indecisive. Arkades, on the other hand, had the potential to actually be a good teacher for Mia. And yet, he’s reduced to a foolish old man brought low by love for his mistress. Also, can we stress that she was just a child when he began to have “feelings” for her??? Any respect I had for his character just disappeared for me after that. <br /><br />The only characters I actually liked in <i>Godsgrave</i> were the other Gladiatii, specially Sid, and Mia’s interaction with them. Although at one point toward the end everyone pretty much started sounding the same. And of course, Mr. Kindly and Eclipse (although can Eclipse please stop calling Mr. Kindly “moggy”?? It sounds pretty ridiculous and I hate it. Up your diss game Eclipse!). <br /> <br /><b>Sexuality:</b> Mia’s bisexuality and subsequent relationship with Ashlinn was actually done pretty well. I like how complex their relationship is and especially in light of the fact that Ash betrayed and then killed Mia’s former lover in book 1. However, despite how complex their relationship is, it is believable and happens quite organically. Moreover, Mia’s love for one does not automatically lessen her love for Tick. They are just two very different relationships between people who have undergone a lot of change in the past year and emerged from that as very different people. I could’ve done without those needlessly long sex scenes though. <br /><br />Less believable was the reveal about Mia’s father. Unlike the reveal about Mia’s mother’s character, where the twist was kind of hinted at in <i>Nevernight</i>, this one seemed a little out of nowhere. In the end, it seemed a little like unnecessary drama added in for pure shock value. <br /><br />I wish they had explained the idea of sexuality more in terms of world building. I’m still unclear about the stance on sexuality taken up in Mia’s world; it’s never really mentioned how people of the LGBTQ community are treated here. Are people of all sexual orientations treated equally? Are there prejudices in place against non-heteronormative individuals? From what I have seen so far, sexuality doesn’t seem to be much of a big deal in this world. Whether you are bisexual like Mia or gay like her father, everyone just seems to roll with it. <br /><br /><b>World building:</b> I have always been very fascinated with ancient Roman culture so the world building works for me. The Gladiatii match on Chariots was a particularly good touch as it showcased how much of this world is influenced by Roman culture. The games were underscored with a sense of dread and desperation; the slaves performing like animals at the circus, highlighting the barbaric nature of the people in power. <br /><br />But slavery itself is not fully explored, despite it being one of the main issues in <i>Godsgrave</i>. Slave culture not fully explored. We are constantly told, rather than shown, that slavery is an issue in <i>Godsgrave</i>; that the master’s exert complete control over their slaves and disobedience is severely punished. And yet, Mia often breaks those rules. She not only talks back to her Donna, but goes so far as to advise, reproach, and even order her around on one occasion. And yet, no punishment is ever doled out for Mia (save for that one time in the beginning). I can understand that since Mia is not a slave, obedience is not something she’s used to. But for the Donna to let her treat her that way seems questionable. It just makes the whole issue with slavery feel very half assed the way it is written, almost as if Mia and the Gladiatii behave as slaves only when it suits the plot. <br /><br /><b>Writing:</b> I generally enjoy Kristoff’s overly dramatic writing style. He has a flair for melodrama and for writing some really good action sequences. There are two standout instances of this in <i>Godsgrave</i>: one, which I already mentioned earlier, was the way he experiments with time in the beginning of the book. The second, is the way in which Kristoff draws parallels while narrating the story. We saw some really beautiful writing in the first chapter of <i>Nevernight</i> when Mia’s sexual encounter is paralleled with her first murder. In <i>Godsgrave</i>, we see the same style of writing when Kristoff describes both Mia and Furian’s having sex with their respective partners, mirroring each other’s actions and dialogues while simultaneously bringing out the contrast between the two couples. It’s beautifully done in both books, and is something that I particularly enjoy about Kristoff’s writing. <br /><br />That and the excess metaphors, I kind of miss them now that Kristoff has toned it down in this book. <br /><br />I do think Kristoff tends to get a bit over dramatic at times. Especially with some of Donna’s high handed manner of speaking that just grated on my nerves. Or maybe that was just her character. But those are minor complaints since I really do enjoy his writing. <br /><br />Overall, 4 stars as I liked this book despite all my criticisms. It is still a vastly entertaining novel and Kristoff's writing keeps you on the edge of your seat, makes it hard to put this book down. I just did not enjoy it as much as <i>Nevernight</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14175557744236727798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2283257510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2103290731210099505"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914778886' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevernight</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2283257510' rel='nofollow noopener'>Godsgrave</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2327040689' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkdawn</a> ???<br/> <br/><b>If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience.</b></blockquote><br/>I don't even know how to start this review. I think I could honestly just write several paragraphs of assorted expletives and shocked/devastated/adoring/amused/enraged/<b>amazed</b> emojis, and it would get the same point across, really. <b>This book is everything I hoped it would be and so much more, and I don't know how I'll ever recover from the traumatizing <i>glory</i> that is this series.</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>The storm begs n</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2103290731210099505" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914778886" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2283257510" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2327040689" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkdawn</a> ???<br /> <br /><b>If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience.</b></blockquote><br />I don't even know how to start this review. I think I could honestly just write several paragraphs of assorted expletives and shocked/devastated/adoring/amused/enraged/<b>amazed</b> emojis, and it would get the same point across, really. <b>This book is everything I hoped it would be and so much more, and I don't know how I'll ever recover from the traumatizing <i>glory</i> that is this series.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>The storm begs no forgiveness of the drowned.</b>
</blockquote><br />Mia Corvere. My sweet, angry, wounded little Crow. I love her so much, on so many different levels and for endless reasons, and she put me through hell in this installment, but I enjoyed every moment of it. Every move she makes is so calculated and brilliant, and I could honestly spend thousands of pages just watching the wheels in her head turn. My heart broke a million times over for her during these chapters, and it's brutal to know that this book was probably nothing compared to what the finale will bring.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“You can keep the glory. I'm just here for the blood.”</b>
</blockquote><br />And the <i>story</i> and <i>pacing</i> in this one! Many trilogies assuredly suffer from the infamous "Middle Book Syndrome", but this is not one of them. If I thought I was on the edge of my seat during <i>Nevernight,</i> that was nothing. Once <i>Godsgrave</i> gets rolling, it brings with it such a whirlwind of action and bloodshed and ruin, you positively can't look away. Despite a terrible reading slump delaying me during the first 20% or so of this book, I think I flew through the last 80% in a few days because it was all I could think about and I found myself reaching for more in every possible free moment I had.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Our scars are just gifts from our enemies... Reminding us they weren't good enough to kill us.”</b>
</blockquote><br />And finally, the <i>romance</i> in this one. If you don't know anything about it, I won't be the one to spoil you, but what a roller coaster. I was spoiled for this particular pairing ages ago, and went into this book wondering how on earth I could possibly root for these characters together, but by the time it came to fruition, I was just as invested as everyone told me I'd be. <b>And Mia's queer rep and questioning?</b> It was <i>everything,</i> watching her slowly piece together why she found herself so fascinated with other women. As another bisexual woman who didn't admit it to myself out until my late teens (hello, Mia, I see you ♥), her journey and realization resonated so soundly with me, I might have even shed a few happy tears. (Thank you, Jay, for telling the story of so many queer ladies like me and Mia, and telling it <i>so damn well.</i>)<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“That’s Fear talking. Never listen to him. Fear is a coward.”</b>
</blockquote><br />There's so much more I want to say, but it would all just be redundant at this point, friends. Let me just say that as far as I'm concerned, <b>this is one of the greatest series ever written, and I can't imagine ever losing the feeling of utter amazement at how <i>beautifully</i> crafted this story, these characters, and this world is.</b> I want to dive right into <i>Darkdawn</i>, and when that's over, I want to start the whole series over — again, and again, and again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2103290731210099505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2712704041?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2019</a>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ✨ A ✨  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/58818027-fares">Fares</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2712704041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15216187261349757381"><b>O, gentlefriends, he has done it again!</b><br/><br/>I'm still a bit in shock of what transpired in the last few chapters. One cannot say that Jay Kristoff does not know how to keep his readers on their toes. <br/><br/><blockquote>In every breath, hope abides.</blockquote><br/><br/><b>
  <u>SPOILERS FOR NEVERNIGHT BOOK 1 BELOW</u>
</b><br/><br/><blockquote>“Conquer your fear,” she whispered, “and you can conquer the world”</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>After the slaughter at the Red Church and the death of Lord Cassius, the Ministry has had to heal from the destruction left behind. Mia is still set on her revenge but n</span>
  <span id="freeText15216187261349757381" style="display:none"><b>O, gentlefriends, he has done it again!</b><br /><br />I'm still a bit in shock of what transpired in the last few chapters. One cannot say that Jay Kristoff does not know how to keep his readers on their toes. <br /><br /><blockquote>In every breath, hope abides.</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>SPOILERS FOR NEVERNIGHT BOOK 1 BELOW</u>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>“Conquer your fear,” she whispered, “and you can conquer the world”</blockquote><br /><br /><br />After the slaughter at the Red Church and the death of Lord Cassius, the Ministry has had to heal from the destruction left behind. Mia is still set on her revenge but now she has more names for her list. The Ministry, although grateful to her for saving them those months ago are not happy with the fact that despite failing her final test, Mia is a fully fledged <i>Blade</i> now, whether they like it or not. <br /><br /><br />Solis, the new Revered Father of the Red Church has banned Mia from going after Julius Scaeva, from going after her revenge. But as we know, Mia is not fond of following instructions. And Ashlyn Jarnheim is back with the biggest explanations and answers to questions Mia didn't even think to ask. <br /><br />Mia is faced with difficult decisions and trials and it was just pheonominal how she dealt with each one. I am under no delusion that Mia is a good person, but she is most definitely a fucking great character to read about. <br /><br />I enjoyed meeting all the new characters. Some I loved (Sidonius) and some made me so mad (Furian). As much as Mia struggled not to form attachments to her new comadrades, so did I. Because as we know, Kristoff has no problem killing off beloved characters and I didn't want to be emotionally attached when that happened. (I failed) <br /><br />Mr. Kindly and Eclipse's banter gave me life! And the footnotes, though much less than they were in NN, were highly entertaining.<br /><br />This book was filled with reveals and plot twists. Some of the theories I had while reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2712701280" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> were revealed and it was still mind blowing. Others came as a complete shock.<br /><br /><br />I am filled with unanswered questions. But the biggest question of all, is whether I'm going to survive the Darkdawn. <br /><br />________<br /><b>My reviews for:</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2712701280" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2712703982" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkdawn</a></span>

  <span id="freeText16034407855618294939" style="display:none"><i>Full review finally up after 16 years</i><br><br>Everytime I think about writing a review for this book my brain goes into full-fledged panic mode <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499330081ra/23217606.gif" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>so here’s my attempt <br><br>-	So godsgrave takes place sometime after nevernights ending<br>-	Mia is still out to get revenge for her familia by any means possible<br>-	Note that in this book mia progresses to get even more bada*s, which yeah, I didn’t think was possible either <br>-	There are more brutal deaths, more blood, more anguish, more deceit and betrayal and friendship and more of your favs dying!!!         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684580168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4588751919284184833">I hate to say it, but I wasn't as captivated during this second read. I'm keeping my rating, though. :)<br/><br/><b>Currently $2.99 on Kindle, August 13, 2019!</b> Also, re-read in progress for the final installment in the trilogy, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23264672.Darkdawn__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___3_' title='Darkdawn (The Nevernight Chronicle, #3) by Jay Kristoff' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkdawn</a>, released on September 3rd!<br/><br/>Update: The MacHalo Blog has a sweepstakes/giveaway for an ARC of Godsgrave with a couple bookish baubles. If you are interested, go <a href='https://dustoffyourmachalo.wordpress.com/2017/10/08/godsgrave-arc-and-bookish-goodies-giveaway/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> to enter. The giveaway ends October 31st at midnight Eastern time.<br/><br/><b>RELEASE DAY! September 5, 2017</b><br/><br/>Review also fou</span>
  <span id="freeText4588751919284184833" style="display:none">I hate to say it, but I wasn't as captivated during this second read. I'm keeping my rating, though. :)<br><br><b>Currently $2.99 on Kindle, August 13, 2019!</b> Also, re-read in progress for the final installment in the trilogy, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23264672.Darkdawn__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___3_" title="Darkdawn (The Nevernight Chronicle, #3) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkdawn</a>, released on September 3rd!<br><br>Update: The MacHalo Blog has a sweepstakes/giveaway for an ARC of Godsgrave with a couple bookish baubles. If you are interested, go <a href="https://dustoffyourmachalo.wordpress.com/2017/10/08/godsgrave-arc-and-bookish-goodies-giveaway/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> to enter. The giveaway ends October 31st at midnight Eastern time.<br><br><b>RELEASE DAY! September 5, 2017</b><br><br>Review also found at the <a href="https://dustoffyourmachalo.wordpress.com/2017/08/26/godsgrave-the-nevernight-chronicles-2-by-jay-kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust Off Your MacHalo</a> blog.<br><br>Book two in The Nevernight Chronicles continues to follow Mia Corvere, darkin assassin, hell bent on revenging her family’s death by order of corrupt tyrannical politicians. While much of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> took place at the Red Church, where Mia competed to become one of the Dark Mother’s blades, this one has a completely new setting and plot. Say bye-bye to the church for a while and hello to this: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503773458ra/23693053.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Without giving too much away, let’s just say Mia finds herself amongst the gladiatii, slaves who fight in arenas as entertainment for blood thirsty audiences.<br><br>Mia’s fellow gladiatii are a wonderful rag-tag crew. We have the brother and sister duo, who fight as a team by chariot. Bladesinger, the bad-ass seven foot tall female who knows how to use her sword. Sidonius is the buddy comedy relief (if there is such a thing in a Jay Kristoff book). Maggot is the young slave who serves as doctor for the group (you don’t want to know why she’s called that). Executus is the ex-gladiatii who leads and trains them (grumpy dude, this guy). Furian is the champion and Mia might have more in common with him than either of them wants. And Dona Leona is their master, the daughter of the leader of the most famous collegium in the Republic, the Lions of Leonides.<br><br>This book is a roller coaster, but I expected no less. Kristoff does not do “beach read” books. He doesn’t do romantic or light and fluffy. No one is safe. Just like the Lotus Wars trilogy and Nevernight, the world-building is complex. Whereas Lotus Wars had a sort of reimagined Japanese steampunk vibe, this has an Italian/Roman vibe. <br><br>So many things happen that I can’t wait to see what those of you who loved Nevernight think. There are (obviously) a few scenes that stand out, and without spoiling, I’ll just say:<br><br>That scene with the retchwyrm.<br>That scene with Ishkah, the silkling.<br>That ending.<br><br>Holy cow, ‘byss and blood. This changes everything.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23264671.Godsgrave__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___2_" title="Godsgrave (The Nevernight Chronicle, #2) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a> is released on September 5, 2017.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503773458ra/23693054.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A special thanks to St. Martin’s press who mailed me this ARC. I adore it, I loved the book, and am a huge fan of Kristoff’s writing (and twisted sense of humor) and of St. Martin’s for publishing awesome books! <br><br>I loved it so much I still have a first-edition signed copy pre-ordered from <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Godsgrave-Book-Two-Nevernight-Chronicle/dp/1250073030/ref=tmm_hrd_swatch_0?_encoding=UTF8&amp;qid=&amp;sr=" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a>.<br><br>My review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1657768507?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a>. FIVE STARS!<br><br><b>Previous post:</b><br>Sometimes, all you have to do is ask. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497996564i/23077988._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you, St. Martin's. You are the best!<br>I can't believe I actually got a PHYSICAL ARC of this. It's Christmas in June! I had to share.<br><br><b>Original post:</b><br><br>Kristoff, I NEED this.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493610148i/22634508.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://jaykristoff.com/2017/03/22/godsgrave-cover-reveal/">https://jaykristoff.com/2017/03/22/go...</a><br><br>I pre-ordered it but I need it before September. :( I hope this goes to Netgalley... sniff sniff.</span>

<div id="review_2083229513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2083229513" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42163117-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508217767p2/42163117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2083229513?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/42163117-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=lgbtqiap-plus">lgbtqiap-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=sapphic">sapphic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2083229513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7260203371997782264">4.75 stars.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>The wolf did not pity the lamb. The storm begged no forgiveness of the drowned.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>It’s rare that a sequel manages to be equally as devastating as the first book. <i>Nevernight</i> was easily one of the best books I’ve read in the last year, but <i>Godsgrave</i> has managed to score a pretty high place up there as well.<br/><br/>I finished this book at 1am, and I genuinely couldn’t sleep because of how much those plot twists fucked me up. Naturally, I ended up making chocolate chip cookies alone in my kitche</span>
  <span id="freeText7260203371997782264" style="display:none">4.75 stars.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The wolf did not pity the lamb. The storm begged no forgiveness of the drowned.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>It’s rare that a sequel manages to be equally as devastating as the first book. <i>Nevernight</i> was easily one of the best books I’ve read in the last year, but <i>Godsgrave</i> has managed to score a pretty high place up there as well.<br><br>I finished this book at 1am, and I genuinely couldn’t sleep because of how much those plot twists fucked me up. Naturally, I ended up making chocolate chip cookies alone in my kitchen in the middle of the night to try to distract myself from my feelings………spoiler alert: <b>IT DIDN’T WORK.</b><br><br><b>Just a note before I continue:</b> if you consider mentioning sexuality and queer characters/relationships to be a spoiler, kindly see yourself out because I am 100% going to be talking about the rep in this series. As a bi woman, knowing about lgbtq+ rep in book is often a huge motivation for me to read it, especially on the wonderful (and unfortunately still rare) occasion that it’s found in my favorite genre—fantasy.<br><br>Moving on—<br><br><i>Godsgrave</i> has a different feel to it than <i>Nevernight</i>. It’s got a similarly dark and twisty plot, with the delightfully original voice, unique world-building, and badass main character that I fell in love with in book 1. But something about this one feels deeper, grittier, and even more deliciously morally gray. If the first book was about revenge and blood and murder school, this one is about revenge and blood and a fucking gladiator competition, with a side of f/f romance and moral conflicts.<br><br>Once again, Mia “you can count the shits I give on no hands” Corvere is a fan-fucking-tastic narrator. She’s on a new path, but her campaign of revenge remains the same: there are still two names on her murder list, after all. She’s smart and strong and vicious, but she’s also painfully human at times. Mia isn’t a caricature of a heartless assassin, she has moments of vulnerability and doubt that make her even more well-developed and compelling.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504894775ra/23841946.gif" width="480" height="442" alt='“arya"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can’t really say much about the plot itself without spoiling anything, but it was possibly even more action-packed, thrilling, and unpredictable than <i>Nevernight</i>'s. I did think the gladiatii plotline was a little slow to start, but once I got into it I found it almost physically impossible to tear myself away from this story. Meeting all of the new characters, learning about the competitions, getting a close-up view of how Itreyan society really works……it was all so <i>interesting</i>. This book does a fantastic job of deepening the complexities of an already-fascinating world. Mia is forced to question the system she grew up in for the first time, to acknowledge how—even after her family fell from grace—she was still immensely privileged.<br><br>The interactions between Mister Kindly and Eclipse were another highlight. The not-cat was a fantastic character in <i>Nevernight</i>, and this book features not one but TWO shadow animal companions that follow along on Mia’s adventures—drinking her fear, spying on people for her, and making snarky comments about her life choices. I’m also still so impressed by how incredible the characterization of two literal shadows was??? Their roles in Mia’s life and their shadowy <s>(hehehe)</s> origins led to some really interesting reflections on their identities, and the mystery of what it really means to be darkin.<br><br><blockquote>
<i>Two passengers met in a dirty alley, in a little city by the sea.<br>The first was small, thin as whispers, cut in the shape of a cat. It had worn the seeming for over seven years now. It could barely remember the thing it had been before. A fraction of a deeper darkness, with only enough awareness to crawl from the black beneath Godsgrave’s skin and seek another like itself.</i> Mia.</blockquote><br><br>As I mentioned before, there’s <b>so much moral gray area!!!</b> Even as Mia sinks further into her revenge scheme, she’s forced to confront the humanity of the people around her, and question the true motives of people she once admired.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>All her life, she’d never questioned the rightness of it. Never stopped to look about her and see the people below her. The folk who’d walked about like voiceless ghosts beneath their home, their apartments in the Ribs. The men and women who’d dressed her, made her meals, taught her numbers and letters. Her mother and father had cared for them, no doubt. Rewarded those who served well. But still, they’d served. Not because they wanted to. Because the alternative was the lash, or death.<br>She felt as if scales were falling from her eyes. The true horror of the Republic she’d been raised inside unveiled in all its awful majesty.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Also !!!!!!! Bisexual and f/f rep!!!!</b> If you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2077227382?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of <i>Nevernight</i></a>, you might remember that I was super excited to find a bi main character in a fantasy series. I really loved that Mia’s sexuality was explored more in this book, both in regards to her attractions towards men and women, and the emotions she had to come to terms with as she realized how much a certain someone truly meant to her (more on this plotline in the spoiler-y section below).<br><br>My only (very, <i>very</i> minor) complaint was that this book did sort of have that “middle of a trilogy” feel to it overall. Don’t get me wrong, I really fucking loved this, but the sense of a bigger picture or any long-term plot seemed to fade away during the gladiatii competition. There are a lot of questions that are still unanswered, a lot that was hinted at for the third book, and the competition didn’t quite feel connected enough to the overall series plot. I also wished we’d gotten to see more of the characters from the first book. The new characters introduced were wonderful as well, but I wished the members of the Red Church ministry, Naev, Adonai, Marielle, Hush, etc.) had gotten more page time. There’s still the third book to look forward to, though, so I’m confident that all of this will pull together into a spectacular conclusion.<br><br><b>A few non-spoilery favorite quotes:</b><br><br><i>Looking out over the mezzanine to the endless shelves below, the girl couldn’t help but smile. She’d grown up inside books. No matter how dark life became, shutting out the hurt was as easy as opening a cover. A child of murdered parents and a failed rebellion, she’d still walked in the boots of scholars and warriors, queens and conquerors.<br>The heavens grant us only one life, but through books, we live a thousand.<br><br>Mia stood over him, pressing her wooden blade to his throat.<br>“Take hold of your fucking jewels,” she said. “Maybe your mother raised you to treat us all as delicate flowers, maybe you’re just thinking with your cock. But there </i>are<i> no girls on the sand. No mothers or daughters. Sons or fathers. Only </i>enemies<i>. You spend a moment worrying about what’s between your opponent’s legs you’ll find your head parted from your body. And what good will your fool cock do you then?”<br><br>“Death is the only promise we all keep. This life we live…there is room in it for love, Mia. But a love like autumn leaves. Beautiful one turn. A bonfire the next. Only ashes the remainder.”</i><br><br><b>SPOILERS EVERYWHERE FROM NOW ON!!!!!!!! GO AWAY NOW IF YOU HAVEN’T READ THIS PLEASE!!!!!!!!!!!</b><br><br>.<br><br>.<br><br>.<br><br>.<br><br>.<br><br>.<br><br>.<br><br>.<br><br>This section is essentially just going to be me screaming about Ash and Mia, you have been warned.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>She thought of Ashlinn then. The kiss they’d shared when Mia left the Church. That kiss that lasted a moment too long. Maybe not long enough?</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Okay, so before I started this book I was talking to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42130592" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a> and I said something along the lines of “wouldn’t it be amazing if Ash gets a redemption arc and she and Mia fall in love?” bc there was lowkey a fair amount of sexual tension between them in <i>Nevernight</i>, but I genuinely didn’t think this would actually happen??? Anyway, we both agreed that yes, this would truly be a fantastic turn of events………so imagine how excited I was when I realized IT WAS ACTUALLY HAPPENING !!!!!!!!! I’m still not over how happy this made me!!!! As a bi girl it’s honestly always amazing to actually get to read about bi girls in an f/f romance!!!!!!! And in a fantasy book no less???? (I apologize for the overuse of punctuation marks but I feel like they are very, very necessary in this case.) Mia and Ash’s relationship was one hell of a friends-to-enemies-to-reluctant-allies-to-lovers plot, and I was here for every second of it.<br><br><blockquote>
<i>“I thought about all the things I could’ve been if I’d been given a choice,” she finally said. “And I realized that mostly I’ve never had one. Ever since my father was killed, my feet were set upon this course. No denying it. No escape. So I wanted to choose something for myself. Something that could be just mine. </i>My<i> choice.”<br>Mia looked at Ash, running trembling fingertips across her cheek. <br>“And I chose you.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444159586ra/16460711.gif" width="480" height="230" alt='“squealing"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And can we talk about Mercurio giving Ash the “you hurt her and I kill you” talk?? Iconic.<br><br><s>Anyway, I’ll stop screaming now.</s><br><br>I would also like to add that the plot twists at the end (both the one that was hinted at in the end of book 1 and the one that was revealed in the last chapter) left me BEYOND shook……all I can say is I better get an ARC of book 3 too bc I don’t think my heart can handle waiting over a year for the rest of Mia’s story.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Dark delight in her belly.<br>Warm blood on her hands.<br>Mia closed her eyes. <br>Raised her blade.<br>Oh Mother, blackest Mother, what have I become?</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>I received an ARC from the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</b><br><br>----------------------------<br><br>do you hear that? it's the sound of me whispering "what the fuck what the fuck what the fuck" to myself over and over again<br><br>----------------------------<br><br>I'm so excited and terrified and I want this book to last forever and I also want to know everything that happens in it <b>RIGHT NOW</b>.<br><br>br with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42130592-kazzy-boy" rel="nofollow noopener">the kinkshamer</a> 💙💙💙</span>

<div id="review_2027246732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2027246732" />
    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2027246732?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027246732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10866270382471997739"><b>Rejoice, O gentlefriends! Devious, gripping and fast paced, Godsgrave has almost everything I expected of this much anticipated sequel and much that was entirely unexpected!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505119210i/23885094._SX540_.jpg' width='800' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><a href='https://goo.gl/x6Bkbr' rel='nofollow noopener'>Truedark Massacre by JujuFei</a><br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Patience, she’d tell herself, whispering the word like a prayer. <br/>If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I have no intentions of discussing the plot in detail, this being the second book, so as to avoid any possible spoilers - Vengeance is ever at the forefront though and consu</span>
  <span id="freeText10866270382471997739" style="display:none"><b>Rejoice, O gentlefriends! Devious, gripping and fast paced, Godsgrave has almost everything I expected of this much anticipated sequel and much that was entirely unexpected!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505119210i/23885094._SX540_.jpg" width="800" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="https://goo.gl/x6Bkbr" rel="nofollow noopener">Truedark Massacre by JujuFei</a><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Patience, she’d tell herself, whispering the word like a prayer. <br>If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I have no intentions of discussing the plot in detail, this being the second book, so as to avoid any possible spoilers - Vengeance is ever at the forefront though and consumes Mia’s thoughts, night and day. The plot continues shortly after the events of Nevernight, and it is a whole new world of dangerous that Mia is subjected to. Where most of the action in Nevernight took place in the Red Church, Kristoff has expanded the playing field exponentially with Mia traveling around quite a bit in her never ending quest for justice. <br><br>Did it entertain? <b>Hell yes! In <i>SPADES. </i></b><br><br>The story starts off with two different timelines, four months apart. The present storyline has you wondering what the hell Mia has gotten herself into, finding herself being sold as a slave to a Collegium of gladiatii or gladiators. The past timeline has her assuming her role as a church Blade, longing for her revenge, yet being held in check by the church for reasons, as of yet, unknown. We get to follow both these timelines until their convergence, where the reasons for Mia’s present quandary are made clear. All of this is of course outlined in the blurb for the story, but I tend to skip reading those before starting a book, so everything was likely more of a mystery to me than it would be to many other readers. The tale was action packed and enthralling, the author's worldbuilding continuing to provide more and more insight into the fascinating place Mia calls home. Pacing presented no issues whatsoever, with those action scenes mentioned being staggered perfectly through the book. And the twistyness, o daughters, the twistyness. Mr Kristoff has shown his true, sly colours. He giveth and he taketh, he is ever so tricky.<br><br>On my first read I felt that this book, whilst compelling and fast paced throughout, never quite reached the level that Nevernight set the bar at. It hovered just below that level throughout most of the story, likely only reaching it and momentarily surpassing it with a <i>pull out all the stops</i> finale. (And WHAT. A. FINALE.) I have changed my mind with this reread though. This book is <i>every bit as good</i>. BUT. I still have a couple (pun gentlefriends, pun.) of things that irk me.<br><br>Firstly, two of the main characters in this book become an item. Though this may be a subterfuge beyond my comprehension on the one character’s part (It's not), I absolutely, unequivocally, HATED IT. In fact, hated sounds too tame. Although being the same thing, <i>
  <b>LOATHED</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>ABHORRED</b>
</i> make better descriptors, for one of these two characters have gone beyond forgiveness in my esteem, and should never, ever have been given even a whiff of the other character’s time of day again, after the events that transpired in Nevernight. Harsh on my part, but I side with the much beloved Mr Darcy here: “My good opinion once lost is lost for ever.'' In fact, the only way the odium* I have attached to this character could be removed is through his or her violent death. I guess my feelings are clear on this point. :) (*Yay! Been wanting to use that word in a sentence ever since Brandon Sanderson made me look it up in the first place!) <br><br>Secondly...see the first reason. AAARGGHHH! I just know I am in the minority with this though.<br><br>At the end of the day, Godsgrave is a superb sequel to Nevernight, holding it's own and then some. I would have gladly given it five stars, had I not taken issue with <i>that</i> relationship. I trust though, that Mr Kristoff will deliver everything I hope for in a final book of what is sure to be a excellent trilogy once completed and I am super excited for what is to come! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“The choice between looking plain and pretty isn't really a choice at all. But any fool knows looking dangerous is preferable to both.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567061861i/28067078._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Image by @phantomrin9<br><br>PS: My hat off to Mr Kristoff on imagining the Retchwyrm - the most disgusting creature I have ever read about. Take a bow, sir. <i>*shudders</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10866270382471997739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2330177644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330177644" />
    <a title="Christian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14731322-christian"><img alt="Christian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571260265p2/14731322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330177644?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christian" href="/user/show/14731322-christian">Christian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14731322-christian?shelf=released-2017">released-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14731322-christian?shelf=better-than-the-rest">better-than-the-rest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330177644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1848618409562252294"><b>Read #2, 2019 - 5 stars</b><br/><br/>Still as neck-twistingly, gut-punchingly and mind-numbingly wild and merciless and unpredictable as the first time around (and this was my second time reading it). I love the layers <i>Godsgrave</i> adds to the series, the new characters it introduces and the phenomenal plot twists it throws your way towards the last 10%. Probably the most unpredictable book I have ever read. I love Mia so, so very much. And while I don't want to let go, I cannot wait to finally read <i>Dardawn</i> afte</span>
  <span id="freeText1848618409562252294" style="display:none"><b>Read #2, 2019 - 5 stars</b><br /><br />Still as neck-twistingly, gut-punchingly and mind-numbingly wild and merciless and unpredictable as the first time around (and this was my second time reading it). I love the layers <i>Godsgrave</i> adds to the series, the new characters it introduces and the phenomenal plot twists it throws your way towards the last 10%. Probably the most unpredictable book I have ever read. I love Mia so, so very much. And while I don't want to let go, I cannot wait to finally read <i>Dardawn</i> after the endless wait. Especially knowing that this story will always be this great, no matter how many times I read it. <br /><br /><b>Read #1, 2018 - 5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>"Dark delight in her belly.<br />Warm blood on her hands.<br />Mia closed her eyes.<br />Raised her blade.<br />'O, Mother, blackest Mother, what have I become?'"</i><br /><br /><br />Back when I wrote down some of my thoughts on <i>Nevernight</i>, my conclusion was that while I thoroughly enjoyed it, there was still a bit of... room for more. More blood, more revenge, more cruelty.<br /><br />Well, something listened. <br /><br />You know how second books in trilogies are often described to suffer from a "second-book-syndrome"? <i>Godsgrave</i> does not. In a way, it almost felt like I was reading the first book in a series, only that it was full of characters I already loved, a world I already knew and mythology I was already familiar with. Which meant that this time, there was no introductory period. It was guts and dubious morality right off the bat, and it was so unbelievably exhilarating. Yet at the same time, we got to see such a different side of Itreya, got to meet so many new characters I got attached to, just to see them killed, hOw FuN. In a way, I guess it felt like I was coming home, but I had just gone decor-shopping and was now redecorating. So, IT WAS AWESOME.<br /><br />This sequel packs exactly the punch I was hoping it would. The new setting and life as a gladiatii is, in a way, even more dangerous and ruthless than the Red Church was, Mia's competitors more unforgiving. And the battle scenes - I'm not gonna lie, they had me breathless most of the time, and even brought tears to my ears occasionally just because they were so intense? It was a strange experience, and one that hit me somewhat unexpectedly. <br /><br />But I am quite certain that the characters are to blame, because at this point, Mia is basically one of my all time favorites, and seeing her constantly putting her life on the line does things to my heart that it does not approve of. She had such a wonderful evolution in this book, started to see darkness beyond the shadows she herself was causing, and once more proved that although she is intent on having her revenge, she remains loyal to those she calls her friends. Also, I don't want to give too much away, but... THE ROMANCE IN THIS? I WAS BLESSED BY AA AND ALL FOUR OF HIS DAUGHTERS. One of my favorites from book 1 returned (as I was desperately hoping they would), and everything progressed so slowly and then unfolded so beautifully and wow. <br /><br />Nonetheless, it never lost sight of bigger plot points, and gave a few hints here and there, obviously without ever giving away too much and setting up most of the bigger reveals for the final installment. (Which will end me.) <br /><br />Another major thing that I absolutely <i>loved</i> and that <i>Godsgrave</i> newly introduced, I feel like, was doubt. First and foremost when it came not only to Mia's own motivations, but also to those of others. And again, not trying to spoil anything here, but there was an impressive amount of gray areas that made it difficult to tell good from bad, hero from villain. I would feel secure in my beliefs one second, only to question them in the next chapter. <br /><br />And finally... I am mad. Mad, because NO ONE seemed to deem it a good idea, maybe, to put a limit to Jay Kristoff and his apparent obsession to destroy his readers with all. These. P L O T T W I S T S. There were just too many turns that I <i>never</i> saw coming, some smaller, some bigger, until that ending... cut my throat to the bone. Ear to ear. Just the way I like it.<br /><br /><i>Godsgrave</i> is what I wanted, mixed with a good amount of stuff I never wanted because it hurt too much, so basically it was all I ever wanted. And my thirst for blood is quenched. For now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1848618409562252294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1757547857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1757547857" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1757547857?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=girl-squad">girl-squad</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well">he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=ripped-my-heart-out">ripped-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=fearless-protagonists">fearless-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=surf-n-turf">surf-n-turf</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=blood-guts-n-gore">blood-guts-n-gore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1757547857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2473278246064345172"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"No matter what you face on those sands, fear is the only enemy in your path. Conquer your fear, and you can conquer the world."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506247163ra/24000186.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The Nevernight Chronicle is, in a nutshell, about a teenage girl <b>mastering new and creative ways to murder people.</b> Last time, it was the art of assassination. This time, it's the way of gladiatii— gladiator.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>What can I say about this series that I haven't thoroughly <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521643502' rel='nofollow noopener'>gushed over</a>? It's <b>gloriously plotted</b>, w</span>
  <span id="freeText2473278246064345172" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"No matter what you face on those sands, fear is the only enemy in your path. Conquer your fear, and you can conquer the world."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506247163ra/24000186.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Nevernight Chronicle is, in a nutshell, about a teenage girl <b>mastering new and creative ways to murder people.</b> Last time, it was the art of assassination. This time, it's the way of gladiatii— gladiator.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"If Vengeance has a mother, her name is Patience."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>What can I say about this series that I haven't thoroughly <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521643502" rel="nofollow noopener">gushed over</a>? It's <b>gloriously plotted</b>, with complex, morally grey characters and a fictional world—complete with extensive history—that keeps expanding book after book like embroidery on a tapestry. <br><br>We learn more about the Republic and the Red Church in Godsgrave, building on the already layered foundation <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> offered. I'm fairly certain I've mentioned this in other reviews, but I <b>love this style of world-building.</b> It's comprehensive without overwhelming, and gives readers a chance to digest information before adding details. (Don't skip the footnotes. Seriously, don't. That's where the fun stuff happens.)<br><br>Readers who felt Nevernight's prose was too purple will be pleased to know Godsgrave dials down on that aspect. While no less absorbing, there are less "weird" metaphors and similes. It's not something I had a problem with, but I know some did. I did feel it got repetitive at times, with Mia constantly reminding herself of her dead family, though that's a minor annoyance.<br><br>Villains are <b>amazing and lovingly written.</b> There are people you're very clearly not supposed to like, such as Leona, owner of Mia's gladiatorial collegium and her slave master. Aside from the obvious (slave owner, yo), she's a proud rich girl who hasn't quite understood she's not rich anymore. But Kristoff invites us to sympathize with her, or at least understand her. <br><br>The ending will kick your mind across the room and play skip-rope with it. A few of the twists I guessed<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[—Jonnen and the rebel gladiatii were obvious, and it makes sense saving the consul for the third and final book— <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>but the final kicker I didn't see coming at all and it fucking nailed my heart to the basement wall. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506247163ra/24000185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506247163ra/24000184.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Some minor things that irked me:</b><br><br>1) Where's Naev?? She and Mia were pretty tight back in the Red Church.<br><br>2) Carlotta deserves a mention. She was a slave and given what Mia experiences, the very least she deserves is a passing thought.<br><br>3) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It really, <i>really</i> pushed the lesbian romance at the expense of Mia's character. Every time she's in the same room as Ashlinn, she's thinking about her curves, her lips, her [insert random sexy body part here]. <br><br>This is the girl who <b>murdered Tric</b>. MURDERED HIM. Mia may not be loyal to the Red Church anymore, but Ashlinn still hurt and betrayed her. I'm not letting her hormones off the hook just because DIVERSITY. <br><br>And they were friends before everything happened. It would have been nice if Mia recalls some of those memories instead of remembering that one time they kissed for the millionth time. Just to be clear, I'm not against Mia/Ashlinn or LGBTQIA relationships in general. In the space of this book, however, I thought the transition from enemy-to-lover could have been written better. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But like I said, they're minor annoyances, and five shimmering stars are sitting on top of this review. I can't recommend this series enough.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506247346ra/24000219.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>P.S. If the third book isn't called Truedark, I'll eat my sweater.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521643502" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Nevernight</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2473278246064345172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mBSpf+qwbep/uUp2FA5aJiajZaxaqNjc8E2+wPQ3YF+hnTKsvyh+U5ta8IGhWnyTjGh3MgLvkpXJy27f0aH4aA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zvtE02STp1QPi+gt8CYUgw84+ADpxQLjLXDwFXlr/I73ct8AMQu07etoUtpFcjI2pfPqnrGCSKoU9iAKXP1kuQ==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText6291831902600432781" style="display:none">Jay Kristoff is a #1 international, New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of fantasy and science fiction. He is as surprised about all of this as you are. He is 6’7 and has approximately 12,000 days to live. <br /><br />He does not believe in happy endings.</span>
